Question 1hard

A parallel plate capacitor has capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is halved and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced between the plates, then the new capacitance becomes:

  1. 2KC
  2. KC/2
  3. C/(2K)
  4. C/(K)
Show answer

Answer: 2KC

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates and d is the distance between them. When the distance is halved, the new capacitance C' = ε₀A/(d/2) = 2(ε₀A/d) = 2C. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the capacitance becomes C'' = KC'. Therefore, the new capacitance is C'' = K(2C) = 2KC.

Question 2hard

Two point charges +q and -q are placed at a distance 'r' from each other. The electric potential at the midpoint of the line joining the two charges is:

  1. 0
  2. kq/r
  3. 2kq/r
  4. -kq/r
Show answer

Answer: 0

The electric potential due to a point charge Q at a distance r is V = kQ/r. At the midpoint, the distance from each charge is r/2. The potential due to +q is V₁ = k(+q)/(r/2) = 2kq/r. The potential due to -q is V₂ = k(-q)/(r/2) = -2kq/r. The total potential at the midpoint is the algebraic sum of the individual potentials: V_total = V₁ + V₂ = (2kq/r) + (-2kq/r) = 0.

Question 3hard

A current of 10 A flows through a conductor for 2 minutes. How much charge passes through any cross-section of the conductor during this time?

  1. 1200 C
  2. 20 C
  3. 120 C
  4. 200 C
Show answer

Answer: 1200 C

The relationship between current (I), charge (Q), and time (t) is given by I = Q/t. Therefore, Q = I × t. Given current I = 10 A and time t = 2 minutes. First, convert time to seconds: t = 2 × 60 = 120 seconds. Now, calculate the charge: Q = 10 A × 120 s = 1200 C.

Question 4hard

Which of the following statements is INCORRECT regarding magnetic field lines?

  1. Magnetic field lines form closed loops.
  2. Magnetic field lines do not intersect each other.
  3. The tangent to a magnetic field line at any point gives the direction of the magnetic field at that point.
  4. Magnetic field lines originate from the south pole and terminate at the north pole.
Show answer

Answer: Magnetic field lines originate from the south pole and terminate at the north pole.

Magnetic field lines originate from the North pole and terminate at the South pole outside the magnet, and inside the magnet, they go from South to North, thus forming continuous closed loops. Options A, B, and C are correct properties of magnetic field lines.

Question 5hard

A metallic rod of length 'L' is rotated with an angular frequency 'ω' with one end hinged at the centre and the other end at the circumference of a circular metallic ring of radius 'R', about an axis passing through the centre and perpendicular to the plane of the ring. A uniform magnetic field 'B' parallel to the axis is present everywhere. The emf induced between the centre and the metallic ring is:

  1. BωR²/2
  2. BωR
  3. BωR²/4
  4. BωL²/2
Show answer

Answer: BωR²/2

The induced emf in a rotating rod in a uniform magnetic field is given by ε = (1/2)BωR², where R is the length of the rod. In this case, the length of the rod is R (radius of the ring). So, the induced emf is ε = (1/2)BωR².

Question 6hard

The phase difference between the alternating current and voltage in a series LCR circuit at resonance is:

  1. 0 degrees
  2. 45 degrees
  3. 90 degrees
  4. 180 degrees
Show answer

Answer: 0 degrees

At resonance in a series LCR circuit, the inductive reactance (X_L) becomes equal to the capacitive reactance (X_C). As a result, the impedance of the circuit becomes purely resistive (Z = R). In a purely resistive circuit, the current and voltage are in phase, meaning the phase difference between them is 0 degrees.

Question 7hard

Which of the following electromagnetic waves has the shortest wavelength?

  1. Radio waves
  2. X-rays
  3. Visible light
  4. Microwaves
Show answer

Answer: X-rays

The electromagnetic spectrum arranges waves by wavelength and frequency. In order of decreasing wavelength (and increasing frequency), the spectrum is: Radio waves, Microwaves, Infrared, Visible light, Ultraviolet, X-rays, Gamma rays. Therefore, X-rays have a shorter wavelength than radio waves, visible light, and microwaves.

Question 8hard

According to Huygens' principle, every point on a wavefront is a source of secondary wavelets which spread out in all directions with the speed of light. The envelope of these secondary wavelets at any instant gives the new position of the wavefront. This principle explains:

  1. Reflection and refraction of light
  2. Diffraction of light
  3. Interference of light
  4. All of the above
Show answer

Answer: All of the above

Huygens' principle is a fundamental concept in wave optics. It successfully explains the phenomena of reflection, refraction, diffraction, and interference of light. It provides a geometrical construction for finding the new position of a wavefront at a later time.

Question 9hard

The work function of a metal is 3.3 eV. Its threshold frequency will be approximately (Given h = 6.6 × 10⁻³⁴ J s):

  1. 8 × 10¹⁴ Hz
  2. 5 × 10¹⁴ Hz
  3. 3 × 10¹⁴ Hz
  4. 1 × 10¹⁴ Hz
Show answer

Answer: 8 × 10¹⁴ Hz

The work function (Φ) is related to the threshold frequency (ν₀) by the equation Φ = hν₀, where h is Planck's constant. First, convert the work function from eV to Joules: Φ = 3.3 eV × 1.6 × 10⁻¹⁹ J/eV = 5.28 × 10⁻¹⁹ J. Now, calculate the threshold frequency: ν₀ = Φ/h = (5.28 × 10⁻¹⁹ J) / (6.6 × 10⁻³⁴ J s) = 0.8 × 10¹⁵ Hz = 8 × 10¹⁴ Hz.

Question 10hard

In a p-n junction diode, the depletion region is formed due to:

  1. Drifting of charge carriers
  2. Diffusion of charge carriers
  3. Recombination of electrons and holes
  4. Both diffusion and recombination of charge carriers
Show answer

Answer: Both diffusion and recombination of charge carriers

The depletion region in a p-n junction diode is formed primarily due to the diffusion of majority charge carriers (holes from p-side to n-side and electrons from n-side to p-side) across the junction. As these carriers diffuse, they leave behind immobile charged ions, creating an electric field. This diffusion leads to the recombination of electrons and holes near the junction, further contributing to the formation and width of the depletion region. So, both diffusion and recombination are key processes.

Question 11hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced completely filling the space between the plates, the capacitance becomes:

  1. KC
  2. C/K
  3. C
  4. K^2C
Show answer

Answer: KC

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates, d is the distance between them, and ε₀ is the permittivity of free space. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the permittivity of the medium becomes ε = Kε₀. Therefore, the new capacitance C' = εA/d = (Kε₀)A/d = K(ε₀A/d) = KC. So, the capacitance increases by a factor of K.

Question 12hard

An electron is accelerated through a potential difference V. Its de Broglie wavelength is λ. If the potential difference is increased to 4V, the new de Broglie wavelength will be:

  1. λ/2
  2. 2λ
  3. λ/4
  4. 4λ
Show answer

Answer: λ/2

The de Broglie wavelength is given by λ = h/p, where h is Planck's constant and p is the momentum. For an electron accelerated through a potential difference V, its kinetic energy is eV. So, 1/2 mv² = eV, which means p = √(2meV). Therefore, λ = h/√(2meV). If the potential difference is increased to 4V, the new wavelength λ' = h/√(2me(4V)) = h/(2√(2meV)) = λ/2. The de Broglie wavelength becomes half.

Question 13hard

A convex lens of focal length f is immersed in water. How does its focal length change?

  1. Increases
  2. Decreases
  3. Remains the same
  4. Becomes zero
Show answer

Answer: Increases

The focal length of a lens is given by the lens maker's formula: 1/f = (n_lens/n_medium - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). When the lens is in air, n_medium = 1. When immersed in water, n_medium = 1.33 (approximately). Since n_water > n_air, the term (n_lens/n_medium - 1) will decrease (as n_lens is typically around 1.5 for glass). A smaller value of this term implies a larger focal length. Thus, the focal length of the convex lens increases when immersed in water.

Question 14hard

Which of the following phenomena confirms the transverse nature of light waves?

  1. Interference
  2. Diffraction
  3. Polarization
  4. Reflection
Show answer

Answer: Polarization

Polarization is the phenomenon that confirms the transverse nature of light waves. Only transverse waves can be polarized, meaning their oscillations can be restricted to a single plane. Longitudinal waves, like sound waves, cannot be polarized because their oscillations are already along the direction of wave propagation. Interference, diffraction, and reflection can occur for both transverse and longitudinal waves.

Question 15hard

The energy of a photon of light with wavelength 500 nm is approximately:

  1. 2.48 eV
  2. 1.24 eV
  3. 4.96 eV
  4. 0.62 eV
Show answer

Answer: 2.48 eV

The energy of a photon is given by E = hc/λ, where h is Planck's constant (6.626 x 10⁻³⁴ J·s), c is the speed of light (3 x 10⁸ m/s), and λ is the wavelength. It's often convenient to use the approximation E (in eV) = 1240 / λ (in nm). So, E = 1240 / 500 = 2.48 eV.

Question 16hard

A current of 1 A flows through a wire of length 1 m and resistance 1 Ω. The potential difference across the wire is:

  1. 1 V
  2. 0.5 V
  3. 2 V
  4. 10 V
Show answer

Answer: 1 V

According to Ohm's Law, V = IR, where V is the potential difference, I is the current, and R is the resistance. Given I = 1 A and R = 1 Ω, the potential difference V = (1 A) * (1 Ω) = 1 V. The length of the wire is extra information not needed for this calculation.

Question 17hard

The phenomenon of electromagnetic induction is described by:

  1. Ampere's Law
  2. Gauss's Law for electricity
  3. Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction
  4. Biot-Savart Law
Show answer

Answer: Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction

Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction states that a changing magnetic flux through a coil induces an electromotive force (EMF) in the coil. This is the fundamental principle behind electromagnetic induction. Ampere's Law relates magnetic fields to electric currents, Gauss's Law for electricity relates electric flux to enclosed charge, and Biot-Savart Law calculates the magnetic field produced by a current element.

Question 18hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of a nuclear force?

  1. It is charge-dependent.
  2. It is the strongest fundamental force in nature.
  3. It is short-ranged.
  4. It is spin-dependent.
Show answer

Answer: It is charge-dependent.

Nuclear forces (strong nuclear force) are primarily charge-independent. They act equally between proton-proton, neutron-neutron, and proton-neutron pairs, apart from the electrostatic repulsion between protons. They are indeed the strongest fundamental force, short-ranged (acting over distances of about 10⁻¹⁵ m), and spin-dependent.

Question 19hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is doubled and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced between the plates, the new capacitance becomes:

  1. KC/2
  2. 2KC
  3. C/(2K)
  4. C/(K)
Show answer

Answer: KC/2

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates and d is the distance between them. When the distance is doubled, the capacitance becomes C' = ε₀A/(2d) = C/2. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the capacitance becomes C'' = K * C' = K * (C/2) = KC/2.

Question 20hard

A straight conductor of length 'L' carrying a current 'I' is placed in a uniform magnetic field 'B' such that the conductor makes an angle 'θ' with the direction of the magnetic field. The magnitude of the magnetic force experienced by the conductor is:

  1. BILsinθ
  2. BILcosθ
  3. BIL
  4. B²IL
Show answer

Answer: BILsinθ

The magnetic force (F) experienced by a current-carrying conductor of length L, carrying current I, placed in a uniform magnetic field B, making an angle θ with the field, is given by the formula F = BILsinθ. This is a fundamental formula in magnetism.

Question 21hard

Lenz's Law is a consequence of the law of conservation of:

  1. Charge
  2. Momentum
  3. Energy
  4. Mass
Show answer

Answer: Energy

Lenz's Law states that the direction of the induced current is such that it opposes the cause that produces it. If it did not oppose the cause, then the induced current would reinforce the change, leading to an ever-increasing current and energy, which would violate the law of conservation of energy. Therefore, Lenz's Law is a direct consequence of the law of conservation of energy.

Question 22hard

In an LCR series circuit, at resonance, the impedance of the circuit is equal to:

  1. R
  2. √(R² + (XL - XC)²)
  3. XL - XC
  4. √(R² + (XL + XC)²)
Show answer

Answer: R

The impedance (Z) of an LCR series circuit is given by Z = √(R² + (XL - XC)²), where R is resistance, XL is inductive reactance, and XC is capacitive reactance. At resonance, XL = XC. Therefore, (XL - XC) = 0, and the impedance becomes Z = √(R² + 0²) = √R² = R. So, at resonance, the impedance is purely resistive.

Question 23hard

A convex lens of focal length 'f' is placed in contact with a concave lens of focal length 'f'. The focal length of the combination is:

  1. 0
  2. f
  3. 2f
  4. infinity
Show answer

Answer: infinity

For a combination of two thin lenses in contact, the equivalent focal length (F) is given by 1/F = 1/f₁ + 1/f₂. Here, f₁ = +f (convex lens) and f₂ = -f (concave lens). So, 1/F = 1/f + 1/(-f) = 1/f - 1/f = 0. This implies F = 1/0, which is infinity. Such a combination acts as a plane glass plate.

Question 24hard

According to Bohr's model, the angular momentum of an electron in a stationary orbit is an integral multiple of:

  1. h/2π
  2. h
  3. 2πh
  4. h/π
Show answer

Answer: h/2π

One of the postulates of Bohr's atomic model states that electrons can revolve only in certain discrete, non-radiating orbits called stationary orbits. In these orbits, the angular momentum of the electron is quantized and is an integral multiple of h/2π, where 'h' is Planck's constant. So, L = n(h/2π), where n = 1, 2, 3, ...

Question 25hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is doubled and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced filling the space between the plates, the new capacitance becomes:

  1. KC/2
  2. 2KC
  3. C/2K
  4. C/K
Show answer

Answer: KC/2

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates and d is the distance between them. When the distance is doubled, the new capacitance C' = ε₀A/(2d) = C/2. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the capacitance becomes C'' = K * C' = K * (C/2) = KC/2.

Question 26hard

A proton and an alpha particle are accelerated through the same potential difference. The ratio of their de Broglie wavelengths (λ_proton : λ_alpha) is:

  1. 1:2
  2. 2√2:1
  3. √2:1
  4. 1:√2
Show answer

Answer: 2√2:1

The de Broglie wavelength is given by λ = h/p, where p is momentum. For a charged particle accelerated through a potential difference V, kinetic energy K = qV. Also, K = p²/2m, so p = √(2mK) = √(2mqV). Thus, λ = h/√(2mqV). For a proton, q_p = e, m_p = m. For an alpha particle, q_α = 2e, m_α = 4m. So, λ_p / λ_α = [h/√(2m_p q_p V)] / [h/√(2m_α q_α V)] = √(m_α q_α / m_p q_p) = √((4m)(2e) / (m)(e)) = √(8) = 2√2. Therefore, λ_proton : λ_alpha = 2√2 : 1.

Question 27hard

In a Young's double-slit experiment, the intensity of light at a point on the screen where the path difference is λ/6 (λ is the wavelength of light) is I. If I₀ is the maximum intensity, then I is equal to:

  1. I₀/2
  2. 3I₀/4
  3. I₀
  4. I₀/4
Show answer

Answer: 3I₀/4

The intensity at a point in Young's double-slit experiment is given by I = I₀ cos²(φ/2), where φ is the phase difference. The phase difference is related to the path difference (Δx) by φ = (2π/λ)Δx. Given Δx = λ/6, φ = (2π/λ)(λ/6) = π/3. So, I = I₀ cos²( (π/3)/2 ) = I₀ cos²(π/6). Since cos(π/6) = √3/2, I = I₀ (√3/2)² = I₀ (3/4) = 3I₀/4.

Question 28hard

A long straight wire carries a current I. A rectangular loop of wire with sides a and b is placed with its longer side parallel to the straight wire at a distance r from it. The mutual inductance between the straight wire and the loop is proportional to:

  1. ln(1 + b/r)
  2. ln(1 + a/r)
  3. ln(1 + a/(r+b))
  4. ln(1 + b/(r+a))
Show answer

Answer: ln(1 + a/r)

The mutual inductance M between a long straight wire and a rectangular loop is given by M = (μ₀a/2π) ln((r+b)/r) = (μ₀a/2π) ln(1 + b/r), where 'a' is the side of the loop parallel to the wire, 'b' is the side perpendicular to the wire, and 'r' is the distance of the closer side from the wire. In this question, the longer side 'b' is parallel to the straight wire, and the shorter side 'a' is perpendicular. So, the formula becomes M = (μ₀b/2π) ln((r+a)/r) = (μ₀b/2π) ln(1 + a/r). Therefore, the mutual inductance is proportional to ln(1 + a/r).

Question 29hard

Which of the following phenomena cannot be explained by the wave nature of light?

  1. Diffraction
  2. Interference
  3. Photoelectric effect
  4. Polarization
Show answer

Answer: Photoelectric effect

Diffraction, interference, and polarization are all phenomena that can be successfully explained by the wave nature of light. However, the photoelectric effect, which involves the emission of electrons from a metal surface when light shines on it, cannot be explained by the wave theory. It requires the particle (photon) nature of light, where light energy is absorbed in discrete packets (quanta).

Question 30hard

A series LCR circuit is connected to an AC source. At resonance, the impedance of the circuit is:

  1. R
  2. √(R² + (XL - XC)²)
  3. XL - XC
  4. R + XL + XC
Show answer

Answer: R

The impedance of a series LCR circuit is given by Z = √(R² + (XL - XC)²), where R is resistance, XL is inductive reactance, and XC is capacitive reactance. At resonance, the inductive reactance (XL) becomes equal to the capacitive reactance (XC), i.e., XL = XC. Therefore, (XL - XC) = 0, and the impedance at resonance simplifies to Z = √(R² + 0²) = R.

Question 31hard

The energy of an electron in the nth orbit of a hydrogen atom is given by E_n = -13.6/n² eV. The energy required to excite an electron from the ground state to the first excited state is:

  1. 13.6 eV
  2. 3.4 eV
  3. 10.2 eV
  4. 1.51 eV
Show answer

Answer: 10.2 eV

The ground state corresponds to n=1, so E₁ = -13.6/1² = -13.6 eV. The first excited state corresponds to n=2, so E₂ = -13.6/2² = -13.6/4 = -3.4 eV. The energy required to excite the electron from the ground state to the first excited state is the difference between these two energy levels: ΔE = E₂ - E₁ = (-3.4 eV) - (-13.6 eV) = 10.2 eV.

Question 32hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of a p-n junction diode in forward bias?

  1. The width of the depletion region decreases.
  2. The potential barrier decreases.
  3. The majority charge carriers move across the junction.
  4. The resistance of the junction increases significantly.
Show answer

Answer: The resistance of the junction increases significantly.

In forward bias, the external voltage opposes the potential barrier, causing it to decrease. This reduction in potential barrier allows majority charge carriers to easily cross the junction, leading to a significant current flow. Consequently, the width of the depletion region decreases, and the resistance of the junction *decreases* significantly, not increases. Therefore, the statement that the resistance increases significantly is incorrect.

Question 33hard

A convex lens of focal length f is placed in contact with a concave lens of focal length f'. The power of the combination is zero. Which of the following is true?

  1. f = f'
  2. f = -f'
  3. f = 2f'
  4. f' = 2f
Show answer

Answer: f = f'

The power of a lens is given by P = 1/f. For a combination of two lenses in contact, the total power P_total = P₁ + P₂. Here, P₁ = 1/f (for convex lens) and P₂ = 1/f' (for concave lens, where f' is typically given as a negative value for a concave lens, but if f' represents the magnitude of the focal length, then P₂ = -1/f'). If the power of the combination is zero, then P₁ + P₂ = 0. So, 1/f + 1/f' = 0. This implies 1/f = -1/f', or f = -f'. However, if f' is already taken as the focal length of the concave lens (which is negative), then 1/f + 1/f' = 0 means 1/f = -1/f'. If we consider the magnitude of focal lengths, then for the power to be zero, the powers must cancel out. A convex lens has positive power (1/f) and a concave lens has negative power (-1/|f'|). So, 1/f - 1/|f'| = 0, which means 1/f = 1/|f'|, or f = |f'|. Therefore, if f' refers to the magnitude of the focal length of the concave lens, then f = f'.

Question 34hard

An electron is accelerated through a potential difference V. Its de Broglie wavelength is proportional to:

  1. V
  2. 1/V
  3. 1/√V
  4. √V
Show answer

Answer: 1/√V

The de Broglie wavelength is given by λ = h/p, where p is the momentum. For an electron accelerated through a potential difference V, its kinetic energy is eV. So, 1/2 mv² = eV, which means p = mv = √(2meV). Substituting this into the de Broglie wavelength formula, λ = h/√(2meV). Therefore, λ is proportional to 1/√V.

Question 35hard

In a Young's double-slit experiment, if the separation between the slits is doubled, the fringe width will:

  1. Be halved
  2. Be doubled
  3. Remain unchanged
  4. Become four times
Show answer

Answer: Be halved

The fringe width (β) in Young's double-slit experiment is given by the formula β = λD/d, where λ is the wavelength of light, D is the distance of the screen from the slits, and d is the separation between the slits. If 'd' is doubled, then β' = λD/(2d) = β/2. Thus, the fringe width will be halved.

Question 36hard

The energy of a photon of wavelength λ is given by:

  1. hc/λ
  2. hλ/c
  3. h/cλ
  4. cλ/h
Show answer

Answer: hc/λ

According to Planck's quantum theory, the energy of a photon (E) is directly proportional to its frequency (ν). So, E = hν, where h is Planck's constant. We also know that the speed of light (c) is related to frequency and wavelength by c = νλ, which means ν = c/λ. Substituting this into the energy equation, we get E = hc/λ.

Question 37hard

Which of the following gates is known as a universal gate?

  1. OR gate
  2. AND gate
  3. NOT gate
  4. NAND gate
Show answer

Answer: NAND gate

NAND and NOR gates are known as universal gates because any other logic gate (AND, OR, NOT, XOR, XNOR) can be constructed using only NAND gates or only NOR gates. This makes them highly versatile in digital circuit design.

Question 38hard

The phenomenon of electromagnetic induction is the production of:

  1. Electric current due to changing magnetic field.
  2. Magnetic field due to changing electric current.
  3. Electric field due to changing magnetic field.
  4. Magnetic field due to changing electric field.
Show answer

Answer: Electric current due to changing magnetic field.

Electromagnetic induction, as described by Faraday's laws, states that a changing magnetic flux through a coil induces an electromotive force (EMF), which in turn drives an electric current if the circuit is closed. Therefore, it is the production of electric current due to a changing magnetic field.

Question 39hard

A proton and an alpha particle are accelerated through the same potential difference. The ratio of their de Broglie wavelengths (λ_p : λ_α) is:

  1. 1:1
  2. √2:1
  3. 2√2:1
  4. 1:2√2
Show answer

Answer: 2√2:1

The de Broglie wavelength is λ = h/√(2m qV). For a proton, mass m_p = m, charge q_p = e. For an alpha particle, mass m_α = 4m, charge q_α = 2e. Since V is the same for both: λ_p / λ_α = [h/√(2m_p q_p V)] / [h/√(2m_α q_α V)] = √(m_α q_α / m_p q_p) = √((4m)(2e) / (m)(e)) = √(8) = 2√2. So, λ_p : λ_α = 2√2 : 1.

Question 40hard

The instantaneous current in an AC circuit is given by I = 2 sin(314t + π/6) A. The RMS value of the current is:

  1. 2 A
  2. √2 A
  3. 1 A
  4. 2/√2 A
Show answer

Answer: √2 A

The instantaneous current in an AC circuit is given by I = I₀ sin(ωt + φ), where I₀ is the peak current. In the given equation, I₀ = 2 A. The RMS (Root Mean Square) value of the current is given by I_rms = I₀/√2. Therefore, I_rms = 2/√2 = √2 A.

Question 41hard

An electron is accelerated through a potential difference V. Its de Broglie wavelength is λ. If the accelerating potential is increased to 4V, the new de Broglie wavelength will be:

  1. λ/2
  2. 2λ
  3. λ/4
  4. 4λ
Show answer

Answer: λ/2

The de Broglie wavelength is given by λ = h/p, where p is the momentum. For an electron accelerated through a potential V, its kinetic energy is eV, so p = √(2meV). Therefore, λ = h/√(2meV). If the potential is increased to 4V, the new wavelength λ' = h/√(2me(4V)) = h/(2√(2meV)) = λ/2.

Question 42hard

Which of the following phenomena is NOT explained by the wave nature of light?

  1. Interference
  2. Diffraction
  3. Polarization
  4. Photoelectric effect
Show answer

Answer: Photoelectric effect

Interference, diffraction, and polarization are all phenomena that can be explained by the wave nature of light. The photoelectric effect, however, demonstrates the particle nature of light (photons) and cannot be explained by classical wave theory.

Question 43hard

A long straight wire carries a current I. A rectangular loop is placed near the wire as shown. If the current in the wire is increasing, the direction of the induced current in the loop will be:

  1. Clockwise
  2. Anticlockwise
  3. No induced current
  4. Depends on the dimensions of the loop
Show answer

Answer: Anticlockwise

According to Ampere's law, a current-carrying wire produces a magnetic field. For a straight wire, the magnetic field lines are concentric circles around the wire. Using the right-hand thumb rule, if the current is upwards, the magnetic field lines inside the loop (closer to the wire) will be directed into the page. As the current I increases, the magnetic flux into the page through the loop increases. By Lenz's law, the induced current will oppose this change. To oppose an increasing magnetic flux into the page, the induced current must create a magnetic field out of the page. Using the right-hand thumb rule again, an anticlockwise current in the loop will produce a magnetic field out of the page. Therefore, the induced current will be anticlockwise.

Question 44hard

The energy of a photon of wavelength λ is E. What is the energy of a photon of wavelength λ/2?

  1. E/2
  2. 2E
  3. E
  4. 4E
Show answer

Answer: 2E

The energy of a photon is given by E = hc/λ, where h is Planck's constant and c is the speed of light. If the wavelength is λ/2, the new energy E' = hc/(λ/2) = 2hc/λ. Since E = hc/λ, then E' = 2E.

Question 45hard

A convex lens of focal length f is placed in contact with a concave lens of focal length f. The equivalent focal length of the combination is:

  1. f
  2. 2f
  3. 0
  4. Infinity
Show answer

Answer: Infinity

The formula for the equivalent focal length (F) of two thin lenses in contact is 1/F = 1/f₁ + 1/f₂. For a convex lens, the focal length is positive (+f). For a concave lens, the focal length is negative (-f). So, 1/F = 1/(+f) + 1/(-f) = 1/f - 1/f = 0. Therefore, 1/F = 0, which implies F = ∞ (infinity). This combination acts like a plane glass plate.

Question 46hard

In a Young's double-slit experiment, if the separation between the slits is doubled and the distance between the slits and the screen is also doubled, the fringe width will:

  1. Remain unchanged
  2. Be halved
  3. Be doubled
  4. Be quadrupled
Show answer

Answer: Remain unchanged

The fringe width (β) in Young's double-slit experiment is given by the formula β = λD/d, where λ is the wavelength of light, D is the distance between the slits and the screen, and d is the separation between the slits. If d is doubled (2d) and D is doubled (2D), the new fringe width β' = λ(2D)/(2d) = λD/d. Thus, the fringe width remains unchanged.

Question 47hard

The energy of a photon of light with wavelength λ is given by:

  1. hc/λ
  2. hλ/c
  3. h/cλ
  4. cλ/h
Show answer

Answer: hc/λ

The energy (E) of a photon is given by E = hν, where h is Planck's constant and ν is the frequency of light. The speed of light (c) is related to frequency and wavelength (λ) by c = νλ, so ν = c/λ. Substituting this into the energy equation, we get E = h(c/λ) = hc/λ.

Question 48hard

Which of the following is a characteristic of a p-n junction diode in reverse bias?

  1. Large current flow
  2. Narrow depletion region
  3. High resistance
  4. Low potential barrier
Show answer

Answer: High resistance

In reverse bias, the positive terminal of the battery is connected to the n-side and the negative terminal to the p-side. This increases the width of the depletion region and the potential barrier, effectively opposing the flow of current. Consequently, the diode offers very high resistance to current flow, and only a very small leakage current flows.

Question 49hard

The SI unit of magnetic flux is:

  1. Tesla
  2. Weber
  3. Henry
  4. Ampere-meter
Show answer

Answer: Weber

Magnetic flux (Φ) is defined as the product of the magnetic field strength (B) and the area (A) perpendicular to the field, i.e., Φ = B⋅A. The SI unit of magnetic field strength (B) is Tesla (T), and the SI unit of area (A) is square meter (m²). Therefore, the SI unit of magnetic flux is Tesla-meter² (T⋅m²), which is also known as Weber (Wb).

Question 50hard

A current-carrying circular loop is placed in a uniform magnetic field. The net magnetic force on the loop is:

  1. Always zero
  2. Always non-zero
  3. Depends on the orientation of the loop
  4. Depends on the magnitude of the current
Show answer

Answer: Always zero

For a closed current-carrying loop placed in a uniform magnetic field, the net magnetic force acting on the loop is always zero. This is because the force on each segment of the loop is given by dF = I(dl x B), and when integrated over the entire closed loop, the vector sum of these forces cancels out, resulting in a net force of zero. However, a torque may act on the loop, causing it to rotate.

Question 51hard

A parallel plate capacitor has a capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is halved and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced filling the space between the plates, the new capacitance will be:

  1. 2KC
  2. KC/2
  3. C/2K
  4. C/K
Show answer

Answer: 2KC

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates and d is the distance between them. When the distance is halved (d' = d/2) and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the new capacitance C' becomes C' = Kε₀A/d'. Substituting d' = d/2, we get C' = Kε₀A/(d/2) = 2K(ε₀A/d). Since C = ε₀A/d, the new capacitance C' = 2KC.

Question 52hard

A proton and an alpha particle are accelerated through the same potential difference. The ratio of their de Broglie wavelengths (λ_p : λ_α) will be:

  1. 1 : 2√2
  2. √2 : 1
  3. 2√2 : 1
  4. 1 : √2
Show answer

Answer: 2√2 : 1

The de Broglie wavelength is given by λ = h/p, where p is the momentum. For a charged particle accelerated through a potential difference V, its kinetic energy K = qV. Also, K = p²/2m, so p = √(2mK) = √(2mqV). Therefore, λ = h/√(2mqV). For a proton: q_p = e, m_p = m. So, λ_p = h/√(2meV). For an alpha particle: q_α = 2e, m_α = 4m. So, λ_α = h/√(2(4m)(2e)V) = h/√(16meV) = h/(4√(meV)). The ratio λ_p : λ_α = [h/√(2meV)] : [h/(4√(meV))] = 1/√(2) : 1/4 = 4 : √2 = 2√2 : 1.

Question 53hard

In a Young's double-slit experiment, the intensity at the central maximum is I₀. If one of the slits is closed, the intensity at the same point will be:

  1. I₀/4
  2. I₀/2
  3. I₀
  4. 2I₀
Show answer

Answer: I₀/4

In Young's double-slit experiment, the intensity at the central maximum (constructive interference) is given by I₀ = (√I₁ + √I₂)² where I₁ and I₂ are the intensities due to individual slits. Assuming the slits are identical, I₁ = I₂ = I. So, I₀ = (√I + √I)² = (2√I)² = 4I. Therefore, I = I₀/4. If one slit is closed, the intensity at that point will be due to the single open slit, which is I. So, the intensity will be I₀/4.

Question 54hard

A series LCR circuit is connected to an AC source. At resonance, which of the following statements is true?

  1. The impedance of the circuit is maximum.
  2. The current in the circuit is minimum.
  3. The voltage across the inductor and capacitor are in phase.
  4. The power factor of the circuit is unity.
Show answer

Answer: The power factor of the circuit is unity.

At resonance in a series LCR circuit, the inductive reactance (X_L) equals the capacitive reactance (X_C). This means the impedance Z = √(R² + (X_L - X_C)²) becomes Z = R (minimum impedance). Consequently, the current in the circuit is maximum. The voltage across the inductor leads the current by 90°, and the voltage across the capacitor lags the current by 90°, so they are 180° out of phase. The power factor, cosφ = R/Z. Since Z=R at resonance, cosφ = R/R = 1 (unity).

Question 55hard

The output of an OR gate is 1 when:

  1. All inputs are 0
  2. Any one input is 0
  3. At least one input is 1
  4. All inputs are 1
Show answer

Answer: At least one input is 1

An OR gate is a digital logic gate that implements logical disjunction. Its output is 1 (true) if one or more of its inputs are 1 (true). The output is 0 (false) only if all of its inputs are 0 (false). So, if at least one input is 1, the output will be 1.

Question 56hard

A current of 1 A flows through a wire of length 0.1 m and resistance 1 Ω. The wire is placed in a magnetic field of 0.5 T perpendicular to its length. The magnitude of the magnetic force experienced by the wire is:

  1. 0.05 N
  2. 0.5 N
  3. 0.1 N
  4. 1 N
Show answer

Answer: 0.05 N

The magnetic force experienced by a current-carrying wire in a magnetic field is given by F = I(L × B). When the wire is perpendicular to the magnetic field, the magnitude of the force is F = I L B sinθ, where θ = 90°, so sinθ = 1. Given: I = 1 A, L = 0.1 m, B = 0.5 T. Therefore, F = (1 A) × (0.1 m) × (0.5 T) = 0.05 N.

Question 57hard

A parallel plate capacitor has capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is halved and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced between the plates, the new capacitance becomes:

  1. C/2K
  2. 2KC
  3. C/K
  4. KC/2
Show answer

Answer: 2KC

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates, d is the distance between them, and ε₀ is the permittivity of free space. When the distance between the plates is halved, the new distance d' = d/2. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the new permittivity becomes ε = Kε₀. So, the new capacitance C' = (Kε₀A) / (d/2) = 2K (ε₀A/d). Since C = ε₀A/d, the new capacitance C' = 2KC.

Question 58hard

A convex lens of focal length 'f' is immersed in a liquid of refractive index greater than that of the lens material. What will be the nature and focal length of the lens in the liquid?

  1. Converging, focal length increases
  2. Diverging, focal length decreases
  3. Converging, focal length decreases
  4. Diverging, focal length increases
Show answer

Answer: Diverging, focal length increases

The lens maker's formula is 1/f = (n_lens/n_medium - 1) (1/R₁ - 1/R₂). For a convex lens in air, n_lens > n_medium (air), so (n_lens/n_medium - 1) is positive, making f positive (converging). When the lens is immersed in a liquid with a refractive index (n_liquid) greater than that of the lens material (n_lens), then n_lens/n_liquid < 1. This makes (n_lens/n_liquid - 1) negative. Therefore, the focal length 'f' becomes negative, indicating that the lens will behave as a diverging lens. Also, the magnitude of (n_lens/n_liquid - 1) will be smaller than (n_lens/n_air - 1), leading to an increase in the magnitude of the focal length (i.e., a weaker lens).

Question 59hard

In a photoelectric effect experiment, the stopping potential depends on:

  1. The intensity of incident light only
  2. The frequency of incident light only
  3. Both the intensity and frequency of incident light
  4. The work function of the metal and the intensity of incident light
Show answer

Answer: The frequency of incident light only

According to Einstein's photoelectric equation, the maximum kinetic energy of emitted photoelectrons is given by KE_max = hν - Φ₀, where h is Planck's constant, ν is the frequency of incident light, and Φ₀ is the work function of the metal. The stopping potential (V₀) is related to the maximum kinetic energy by KE_max = eV₀. Therefore, eV₀ = hν - Φ₀, or V₀ = (h/e)ν - (Φ₀/e). This equation shows that the stopping potential (V₀) depends linearly on the frequency (ν) of the incident light and the work function (Φ₀) of the metal. It does not depend on the intensity of the incident light, as intensity only affects the number of emitted photoelectrons, not their maximum kinetic energy.

Question 60hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If the space between the plates is now filled with a dielectric material of dielectric constant K, and the capacitor is connected to a battery of voltage V, which of the following statements is INCORRECT?

  1. The capacitance of the capacitor increases to KC.
  2. The charge stored on the capacitor increases to KQ.
  3. The electric field between the plates remains the same.
  4. The energy stored in the capacitor increases to K times its initial value.
Show answer

Answer: The electric field between the plates remains the same.

Let the initial capacitance be C, initial charge be Q, initial electric field be E, and initial energy be U. When the capacitor is connected to a battery, the potential difference V across its plates remains constant. 1. **Capacitance:** When a dielectric of constant K is introduced, the capacitance increases. The new capacitance C' = KC. So, statement (A) is correct. 2. **Charge:** Since C' = KC and V remains constant, the new charge Q' = C'V = (KC)V = K(CV) = KQ. So, statement (B) is correct. 3. **Electric Field:** The electric field between the plates is given by E = V/d, where d is the distance between the plates. Since V (potential difference) and d (distance) remain constant, the electric field E between the plates also remains the same. However, the question asks for the INCORRECT statement. Let's re-evaluate this. When a dielectric is introduced, the electric field *inside* the dielectric due to the *free charges* on the plates remains E0 = V/d. But the dielectric itself gets polarized, creating an induced electric field in the opposite direction. The *net* electric field inside the dielectric is E = E0/K = V/(Kd). Therefore, the electric field *decreases* by a factor of K. So, statement (C) is incorrect. 4. **Energy Stored:** The initial energy stored is U = (1/2)CV^2. The new energy stored is U' = (1/2)C'V^2 = (1/2)(KC)V^2 = K * (1/2)CV^2 = KU. So, statement (D) is correct. Therefore, the incorrect statement is that the electric field between the plates remains the same.

Question 61hard

A long straight conductor carries a current of 2A. The magnetic field at a distance of 10 cm from the conductor is:

  1. 4 × 10⁻⁶ T
  2. 4 × 10⁻⁵ T
  3. 2 × 10⁻⁶ T
  4. 2 × 10⁻⁵ T
Show answer

Answer: 4 × 10⁻⁶ T

The magnetic field (B) due to a long straight current-carrying conductor at a distance r is given by the formula B = (μ₀I) / (2πr). Given: Current I = 2A, Distance r = 10 cm = 0.1 m. Permeability of free space μ₀ = 4π × 10⁻⁷ T m/A. Substitute the values into the formula: B = (4π × 10⁻⁷ T m/A × 2A) / (2π × 0.1 m) B = (8π × 10⁻⁷) / (0.2π) B = (8 × 10⁻⁷) / 0.2 B = 40 × 10⁻⁷ T = 4 × 10⁻⁶ T.

Question 62hard

Which of the following is a correct statement about p-n junction diode in reverse bias?

  1. The depletion region width decreases.
  2. The potential barrier decreases.
  3. The majority charge carriers flow across the junction.
  4. A small reverse current flows due to minority charge carriers.
Show answer

Answer: A small reverse current flows due to minority charge carriers.

In reverse bias, the positive terminal of the battery is connected to the n-side and the negative terminal to the p-side. This increases the potential barrier and widens the depletion region, opposing the flow of majority charge carriers. However, a very small current, known as reverse saturation current, flows due to the drift of minority charge carriers across the junction. Options A, B, and C are incorrect for reverse bias.

Question 63hard

The instantaneous voltage and current in an AC circuit are given by V = 100 sin(314t) V and I = 5 sin(314t - π/3) A. The power factor of the circuit is:

  1. 0.5
  2. 0.866
  3. 1.0
  4. 0.707
Show answer

Answer: 0.5

The power factor (cos φ) of an AC circuit is given by the cosine of the phase difference (φ) between the voltage and current. From the given equations: V = 100 sin(314t) V, so the phase of voltage is 0. I = 5 sin(314t - π/3) A, so the phase of current is -π/3. The phase difference φ = (phase of voltage) - (phase of current) = 0 - (-π/3) = π/3 radians. Power factor = cos(φ) = cos(π/3). We know that cos(π/3) = cos(60°) = 0.5. Therefore, the power factor of the circuit is 0.5.

Question 64hard

Which of the following statements is INCORRECT regarding electric field lines?

  1. Electric field lines originate from positive charges and terminate on negative charges.
  2. Two electric field lines can never cross each other.
  3. The tangent to an electric field line at any point gives the direction of the electric field at that point.
  4. Electric field lines form closed loops.
Show answer

Answer: Electric field lines form closed loops.

Electric field lines do not form closed loops. They originate from positive charges and terminate on negative charges (or extend to infinity). Magnetic field lines, on the other hand, form closed loops.

Question 65hard

A wire of resistance R is stretched to twice its original length. Assuming that its volume remains unchanged, its new resistance will be:

  1. R/2
  2. 2R
  3. 4R
  4. R
Show answer

Answer: 4R

Let the original length be L and cross-sectional area be A. The original resistance R = ρL/A. When the wire is stretched to twice its original length (L' = 2L), its volume (V = AL) remains unchanged. So, A'L' = AL, which means A'(2L) = AL, so A' = A/2. The new resistance R' = ρL'/A' = ρ(2L)/(A/2) = 4(ρL/A) = 4R.

Question 66hard

In Young's double-slit experiment, if the separation between the slits is doubled and the distance between the slits and the screen is also doubled, the fringe width will:

  1. remain unchanged
  2. be halved
  3. be doubled
  4. be quadrupled
Show answer

Answer: remain unchanged

The fringe width (β) in Young's double-slit experiment is given by β = λD/d, where λ is the wavelength of light, D is the distance between the slits and the screen, and d is the separation between the slits. If d becomes 2d and D becomes 2D, the new fringe width β' = λ(2D)/(2d) = λD/d = β. Thus, the fringe width remains unchanged.

Question 67hard

The magnetic field at the centre of a current-carrying circular coil of radius R is B. What will be the magnetic field at the centre if the current is doubled and the radius is halved?

  1. B
  2. 2B
  3. 4B
  4. 8B
Show answer

Answer: 8B

The magnetic field at the centre of a current-carrying circular coil is given by B = (μ₀I)/(2R). If the current I is doubled (I' = 2I) and the radius R is halved (R' = R/2), the new magnetic field B' = (μ₀(2I))/(2(R/2)) = (μ₀2I)/(R) = 4(μ₀I)/(2R) = 4B. So, the magnetic field becomes 4 times the original value.

Question 68hard

A coil of area A and N turns is placed in a uniform magnetic field B with its plane perpendicular to the field. The magnetic flux linked with the coil is:

  1. NBA
  2. NBAcosθ
  3. NBAsinθ
  4. zero
Show answer

Answer: NBA

The magnetic flux (Φ) linked with a single turn of a coil is given by Φ = B⋅A = BAcosθ, where θ is the angle between the magnetic field vector (B) and the area vector (A). When the plane of the coil is perpendicular to the magnetic field, the area vector is parallel to the magnetic field, so θ = 0°. Thus, cosθ = 1. For N turns, the total magnetic flux linked with the coil is Φ_total = NΦ = NBA.

Question 69hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is doubled and the space between the plates is filled with a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K=4, the new capacitance will be:

  1. C
  2. 2C
  3. 4C
  4. 8C
Show answer

Answer: 2C

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates and d is the distance between them. When the distance is doubled, the capacitance becomes C' = ε₀A/(2d) = C/2. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the capacitance becomes C'' = K * C'. So, C'' = 4 * (C/2) = 2C.

Question 70hard

A proton and an electron are accelerated through the same potential difference. Which of the following quantities will be the same for both?

  1. Kinetic energy
  2. Momentum
  3. Speed
  4. De Broglie wavelength
Show answer

Answer: Kinetic energy

When a charged particle (charge q) is accelerated through a potential difference V, its kinetic energy (KE) gained is given by KE = qV. Since both the proton and electron have the same magnitude of charge (e) and are accelerated through the same potential difference V, their kinetic energies will be the same (KE = eV). Their masses are different, so their momentum, speed, and de Broglie wavelength will be different.

Question 71hard

A convex lens of focal length 'f' is immersed in a liquid of refractive index greater than that of the lens material. The lens will behave as a:

  1. Convex lens of shorter focal length
  2. Convex lens of longer focal length
  3. Concave lens
  4. Plane glass plate
Show answer

Answer: Concave lens

The lens maker's formula is 1/f = (n_lens/n_medium - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). If n_medium > n_lens, then (n_lens/n_medium - 1) becomes negative. For a convex lens in air (n_medium < n_lens), (n_lens/n_medium - 1) is positive, resulting in a positive focal length. When immersed in a denser medium, the term becomes negative, making the focal length negative, which means the convex lens will behave as a concave lens.

Question 72hard

A current of 1 A flows through a wire of length 1 m and resistance 1 Ω. The potential difference across the ends of the wire is:

  1. 1 V
  2. 0.5 V
  3. 2 V
  4. 10 V
Show answer

Answer: 1 V

According to Ohm's Law, the potential difference (V) across a conductor is directly proportional to the current (I) flowing through it and its resistance (R). The formula is V = IR. Given I = 1 A and R = 1 Ω, V = (1 A) * (1 Ω) = 1 V.

Question 73hard

The half-life of a radioactive substance is 20 minutes. What fraction of the original activity will remain after 1 hour?

  1. 1/2
  2. 1/4
  3. 1/8
  4. 1/16
Show answer

Answer: 1/8

The half-life (T₁/₂) is 20 minutes. The total time elapsed is 1 hour = 60 minutes. The number of half-lives (n) is total time / half-life = 60 minutes / 20 minutes = 3. The fraction of the original activity remaining after 'n' half-lives is (1/2)^n. So, after 3 half-lives, the fraction remaining is (1/2)³ = 1/8.

Question 74hard

Which of the following is the correct order of electromagnetic waves in increasing order of wavelength?

  1. Gamma rays, X-rays, Ultraviolet, Visible, Infrared, Microwaves, Radio waves
  2. Radio waves, Microwaves, Infrared, Visible, Ultraviolet, X-rays, Gamma rays
  3. Visible, Ultraviolet, X-rays, Gamma rays, Infrared, Microwaves, Radio waves
  4. Gamma rays, Radio waves, X-rays, Visible, Ultraviolet, Infrared, Microwaves
Show answer

Answer: Gamma rays, X-rays, Ultraviolet, Visible, Infrared, Microwaves, Radio waves

The electromagnetic spectrum is ordered by wavelength (or frequency). In increasing order of wavelength (and decreasing order of frequency/energy), the sequence is: Gamma rays, X-rays, Ultraviolet, Visible light, Infrared, Microwaves, Radio waves.

Question 75hard

A convex lens of focal length f is immersed in a liquid of refractive index greater than that of the lens. The lens will behave as a:

  1. Converging lens of shorter focal length
  2. Diverging lens
  3. Converging lens of longer focal length
  4. Plane glass plate
Show answer

Answer: Diverging lens

The lens maker's formula is 1/f = (n_lens/n_medium - 1)(1/R1 - 1/R2). If n_medium > n_lens, then (n_lens/n_medium - 1) becomes negative. For a convex lens in air (n_medium < n_lens), (n_lens/n_medium - 1) is positive, making f positive (converging). When n_medium > n_lens, the term (n_lens/n_medium - 1) becomes negative, which makes the focal length f negative. A negative focal length indicates a diverging lens.

Question 76hard

A current of 1 A flows through a conductor for 1 minute. How many electrons pass through any cross-section of the conductor during this time?

  1. 6.25 × 10¹⁸
  2. 3.75 × 10²⁰
  3. 6.25 × 10²⁰
  4. 3.75 × 10¹⁸
Show answer

Answer: 3.75 × 10²⁰

Current I = Q/t, so Q = I × t. Given I = 1 A and t = 1 minute = 60 seconds. So, Q = 1 A × 60 s = 60 C. The charge of one electron (e) is 1.6 × 10⁻¹⁹ C. The number of electrons (n) is Q/e = 60 C / (1.6 × 10⁻¹⁹ C/electron) = 37.5 × 10¹⁹ electrons = 3.75 × 10²⁰ electrons.

Question 77hard

Which of the following phenomena is responsible for the blue color of the sky?

  1. Reflection
  2. Refraction
  3. Dispersion
  4. Scattering
Show answer

Answer: Scattering

The blue color of the sky is due to Rayleigh scattering. Shorter wavelengths (like blue light) are scattered more effectively by the small particles (molecules of air) in the atmosphere than longer wavelengths (like red light). This scattered blue light reaches our eyes from all directions, making the sky appear blue.

Question 78hard

A step-up transformer increases the AC voltage. What happens to the AC current in the secondary coil compared to the primary coil, assuming an ideal transformer?

  1. It increases.
  2. It decreases.
  3. It remains the same.
  4. It becomes zero.
Show answer

Answer: It decreases.

For an ideal transformer, the power in the primary coil is equal to the power in the secondary coil (P_primary = P_secondary). Since P = VI, we have V_pI_p = V_sI_s. In a step-up transformer, V_s > V_p. To maintain the equality of power, I_s must be less than I_p. Therefore, the current in the secondary coil decreases.

Question 79hard

A convex lens of focal length 'f' is immersed in water. How will its focal length change?

  1. Increase
  2. Decrease
  3. Remain unchanged
  4. Become zero
Show answer

Answer: Increase

The focal length of a lens depends on the refractive index of the lens material and the surrounding medium. The lens maker's formula is 1/f = (n_lens/n_medium - 1)(1/R1 - 1/R2). When the lens is immersed in water (n_water > n_air), the ratio (n_lens/n_medium) decreases. Since n_lens is typically greater than n_water, the term (n_lens/n_medium - 1) decreases, leading to an increase in the focal length of the convex lens.

Question 80hard

The energy of an electron in the nth orbit of a hydrogen atom is given by E_n = -13.6/n² eV. What is the energy required to excite an electron from the ground state to the first excited state?

  1. 13.6 eV
  2. 3.4 eV
  3. 10.2 eV
  4. 1.51 eV
Show answer

Answer: 10.2 eV

The ground state corresponds to n=1, so E₁ = -13.6/1² = -13.6 eV. The first excited state corresponds to n=2, so E₂ = -13.6/2² = -13.6/4 = -3.4 eV. The energy required to excite the electron is the difference between these two energy levels: ΔE = E₂ - E₁ = -3.4 eV - (-13.6 eV) = 10.2 eV.

Question 81hard

A current of 1 A flows through a wire of length 0.1 m placed in a uniform magnetic field of 0.5 T. If the wire makes an angle of 30° with the magnetic field, the magnetic force on the wire is:

  1. 0.025 N
  2. 0.05 N
  3. 0.0025 N
  4. 0.005 N
Show answer

Answer: 0.025 N

The magnetic force on a current-carrying wire in a uniform magnetic field is given by F = I(L × B) = I L B sinθ. Given I = 1 A, L = 0.1 m, B = 0.5 T, and θ = 30°. So, F = 1 × 0.1 × 0.5 × sin(30°) = 0.1 × 0.5 × 0.5 = 0.025 N.

Question 82hard

Which of the following is a correct statement about p-n junction diode?

  1. In forward bias, the depletion region width increases.
  2. In reverse bias, the potential barrier decreases.
  3. In forward bias, the majority carriers move across the junction.
  4. In reverse bias, a large current flows due to majority carriers.
Show answer

Answer: In forward bias, the majority carriers move across the junction.

In forward bias, the external voltage opposes the potential barrier, reducing its height and the depletion region width. This allows majority carriers to easily cross the junction, leading to a significant current. In reverse bias, the external voltage adds to the potential barrier, increasing its height and the depletion region width, and only a very small leakage current flows due to minority carriers.

Question 83hard

A proton and an alpha particle are accelerated through the same potential difference. The ratio of their final kinetic energies (K_proton : K_alpha) is:

  1. 1:1
  2. 1:2
  3. 2:1
  4. 1:4
Show answer

Answer: 1:2

The kinetic energy gained by a charged particle accelerated through a potential difference V is given by K = qV, where q is the charge of the particle. For a proton, charge q_p = +e. So, K_p = eV. For an alpha particle, charge q_α = +2e. So, K_α = (2e)V = 2eV. Therefore, the ratio K_p : K_α = eV : 2eV = 1:2.

Question 84hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of a ferromagnetic material?

  1. They exhibit strong attraction to magnets.
  2. They retain magnetism even after the external magnetic field is removed.
  3. Their magnetic susceptibility is small and positive.
  4. They have distinct magnetic domains.
Show answer

Answer: Their magnetic susceptibility is small and positive.

Ferromagnetic materials have a large and positive magnetic susceptibility (χ_m >> 1). Diamagnetic materials have small and negative susceptibility, while paramagnetic materials have small and positive susceptibility. Ferromagnetic materials are strongly attracted to magnets, exhibit hysteresis (retaining magnetism), and are characterized by magnetic domains.

Question 85hard

The energy of a photon of wavelength λ is E. The energy of a photon of wavelength λ/2 will be:

  1. E/2
  2. 2E
  3. E
  4. 4E
Show answer

Answer: 2E

The energy of a photon is given by E = hc/λ, where h is Planck's constant and c is the speed of light. If the wavelength is λ/2, the new energy E' = hc/(λ/2) = 2(hc/λ) = 2E.

Question 86hard

A convex lens of focal length f is immersed in water (refractive index 4/3). If the refractive index of the material of the lens is 3/2, its focal length in water will be:

  1. f
  2. 2f
  3. 4f
  4. f/2
Show answer

Answer: 4f

The lens maker's formula is 1/f = (n_lens/n_medium - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). In air (n_medium = 1): 1/f_air = (n_lens - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂) = (3/2 - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂) = (1/2)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). In water (n_medium = 4/3): 1/f_water = ( (3/2) / (4/3) - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂) = (9/8 - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂) = (1/8)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). Dividing the two equations: (1/f_water) / (1/f_air) = (1/8) / (1/2) = 1/4. So, f_air / f_water = 1/4, which means f_water = 4 * f_air. Given f_air = f, so f_water = 4f.

Question 87hard

  2. Visible light, Infrared, Microwaves, Radio waves
  3. Infrared, Visible light, Microwaves, Radio waves
  4. Microwaves, Radio waves, Visible light, Infrared
Show answer

Answer: Radio waves, Microwaves, Infrared, Visible light

The electromagnetic spectrum in order of increasing frequency (and decreasing wavelength) is: Radio waves, Microwaves, Infrared, Visible light, Ultraviolet, X-rays, Gamma rays. Therefore, the correct order for the given options is Radio waves, Microwaves, Infrared, Visible light.

Question 89hard

The phenomenon of light bending around corners or obstacles is called:

  1. Reflection
  2. Refraction
  3. Diffraction
  4. Interference
Show answer

Answer: Diffraction

Diffraction is the phenomenon where light waves bend around obstacles or spread out after passing through a small opening. Reflection is the bouncing back of light, refraction is the bending of light as it passes from one medium to another, and interference is the superposition of two or more waves resulting in a new wave pattern.

Question 90hard

Which of the following materials is suitable for making the core of an electromagnet?

  1. Steel
  2. Copper
  3. Soft iron
  4. Aluminium
Show answer

Answer: Soft iron

Soft iron is suitable for making the core of an electromagnet because it has high magnetic permeability and low retentivity. This means it can be easily magnetized when current flows through the coil and easily demagnetized when the current is switched off, which is essential for an electromagnet. Steel has high retentivity, making it suitable for permanent magnets. Copper and aluminium are non-magnetic materials.

Question 91hard

According to Kirchhoff's first law (junction rule), the algebraic sum of currents meeting at any junction in an electrical circuit is:

  1. Always positive
  2. Always negative
  3. Zero
  4. Dependent on the resistance of the circuit
Show answer

Answer: Zero

Kirchhoff's first law, also known as the junction rule or current law, states that the algebraic sum of currents entering a junction is equal to the algebraic sum of currents leaving the junction. This is a statement of conservation of charge. Therefore, the net algebraic sum of currents meeting at any junction is zero.

Question 92hard

The energy of a photon is given by E = hν, where h is Planck's constant and ν is the frequency of the light. If the wavelength of light is λ, then the energy can also be expressed as:

  1. hc/λ
  2. hλ/c
  3. h/cλ
  4. c/hλ
Show answer

Answer: hc/λ

The relationship between the speed of light (c), frequency (ν), and wavelength (λ) is c = νλ. From this, we can express frequency as ν = c/λ. Substituting this into the energy equation E = hν, we get E = h(c/λ) = hc/λ.

Question 93hard

Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of electromagnetic waves?

  1. They are transverse in nature.
  2. They can travel through a vacuum.
  3. They require a material medium for propagation.
  4. They travel with the speed of light in vacuum.
Show answer

Answer: They require a material medium for propagation.

Electromagnetic waves are transverse waves, meaning their electric and magnetic field oscillations are perpendicular to the direction of propagation. They do not require a material medium for propagation and can travel through a vacuum. In a vacuum, all electromagnetic waves travel at the speed of light (c ≈ 3 x 10⁸ m/s). Therefore, the statement that they require a material medium for propagation is incorrect.

Question 94hard

A convex lens of focal length 20 cm is placed in contact with a concave lens of focal length 25 cm. The power of the combination is:

  1. +1 D
  2. -1 D
  3. +9 D
  4. -9 D
Show answer

Answer: +1 D

The power of a lens is given by P = 1/f (in meters). For the convex lens, f₁ = +20 cm = +0.20 m. So, P₁ = 1/0.20 = +5 D. For the concave lens, f₂ = -25 cm = -0.25 m. So, P₂ = 1/(-0.25) = -4 D. The power of the combination (P_comb) is the algebraic sum of the individual powers: P_comb = P₁ + P₂ = +5 D + (-4 D) = +1 D.

Question 95hard

In a Young's double-slit experiment, the intensity at the central maximum is I₀. What is the intensity at a point where the path difference is λ/4?

  1. I₀/2
  2. I₀/√2
  3. I₀/4
  4. 3I₀/4
Show answer

Answer: I₀/2

The intensity at any point in Young's double-slit experiment is given by I = I₀ cos²(φ/2), where φ is the phase difference. The phase difference is related to the path difference Δx by φ = (2π/λ)Δx. Given Δx = λ/4, then φ = (2π/λ)(λ/4) = π/2. So, I = I₀ cos²( (π/2)/2 ) = I₀ cos²(π/4) = I₀ (1/√2)² = I₀/2.

Question 97hard

  1. 0°
  2. 45°
  3. 90°
  4. 180°
Show answer

Answer: 90°

The force experienced by a current-carrying conductor in a uniform magnetic field is given by F = BILsinθ, where θ is the angle between the direction of the current and the magnetic field. The force is maximum when sinθ is maximum, which occurs when θ = 90° (sin 90° = 1).

Question 98hard

  2. Compton effect
  3. Interference
  4. Blackbody radiation
Show answer

Photoelectric effect, Compton effect, and blackbody radiation are phenomena that support the particle nature of light (photon concept).

  1. 20 C
  2. 120 C
  3. 1200 C
  4. 2400 C
Show answer

Answer: 1200 C

Question 100hard

A step-up transformer increases the AC voltage. What happens to the current in the secondary coil compared to the primary coil?

  1. It increases.
  2. It decreases.
  3. It remains the same.
  4. It becomes zero.
Show answer

Answer: It decreases.

For an ideal transformer, the power in the primary coil is equal to the power in the secondary coil (P_primary = P_secondary). Since P = VI, we have V_p I_p = V_s I_s. In a step-up transformer, V_s > V_p. To maintain the equality of power, I_s must be less than I_p. Therefore, the current in the secondary coil decreases.

Question 101hard

A long straight wire carries a current I. A rectangular loop is placed near the wire as shown in the figure. If the current in the wire is increasing, the direction of the induced current in the loop will be:

  1. Clockwise
  2. Anti-clockwise
  3. No induced current
  4. Depends on the dimensions of the loop
Show answer

Answer: Anti-clockwise

According to Ampere's law, the magnetic field produced by a long straight current-carrying wire is B = μ₀I/(2πr). Using the right-hand thumb rule, if the current I is upwards, the magnetic field lines inside the loop (closer to the wire) will be directed into the page. As the current I is increasing, the magnetic flux into the page through the loop is increasing. By Lenz's Law, the induced current in the loop will oppose this change. To oppose an increasing inward flux, the induced current must produce an outward magnetic field. Using the right-hand thumb rule again, an anti-clockwise current in the loop will produce an outward magnetic field. Therefore, the induced current will be anti-clockwise.

Question 102hard

The energy of an electron in the nth orbit of hydrogen atom is given by E_n = -13.6/n² eV. The energy required to excite an electron from the ground state to the first excited state is:

  1. 13.6 eV
  2. 3.4 eV
  3. 10.2 eV
  4. 1.51 eV
Show answer

Answer: 10.2 eV

The ground state corresponds to n=1, so E₁ = -13.6/1² = -13.6 eV. The first excited state corresponds to n=2, so E₂ = -13.6/2² = -13.6/4 = -3.4 eV. The energy required to excite the electron from the ground state to the first excited state is the difference between these two energy levels: ΔE = E₂ - E₁ = (-3.4 eV) - (-13.6 eV) = 10.2 eV.

Question 103hard

A current of 2A flows in a conductor of resistance 4Ω. The power dissipated in the conductor is:

  1. 8 W
  2. 16 W
  3. 2 W
  4. 4 W
Show answer

Answer: 16 W

The power dissipated in a conductor is given by the formula P = I²R, where I is the current and R is the resistance. Given I = 2A and R = 4Ω. So, P = (2A)² * 4Ω = 4 * 4 = 16 W.

Question 105hard

The work function of a metal is 3.3 eV. The threshold frequency for photoelectric emission from this metal is approximately (Given h = 6.6 × 10⁻³⁴ J s, 1 eV = 1.6 × 10⁻¹⁹ J):

  1. 8 × 10¹⁴ Hz
  2. 5 × 10¹⁴ Hz
  3. 2 × 10¹⁴ Hz
  4. 1 × 10¹⁴ Hz
Show answer

Answer: 8 × 10¹⁴ Hz

The work function (Φ) is related to the threshold frequency (ν₀) by the equation Φ = hν₀. We are given Φ = 3.3 eV. First, convert eV to Joules: Φ = 3.3 × 1.6 × 10⁻¹⁹ J = 5.28 × 10⁻¹⁹ J. Now, ν₀ = Φ / h = (5.28 × 10⁻¹⁹ J) / (6.6 × 10⁻³⁴ J s) = (5.28 / 6.6) × 10¹⁵ Hz = 0.8 × 10¹⁵ Hz = 8 × 10¹⁴ Hz.

Question 106hard

The half-life of a radioactive substance is 20 minutes. The time taken for 75% of the substance to disintegrate is:

  1. 10 minutes
  2. 20 minutes
  3. 30 minutes
  4. 40 minutes
Show answer

Answer: 40 minutes

After one half-life (T₁/₂), 50% of the substance remains. After two half-lives (2T₁/₂), 50% of the remaining 50% (i.e., 25% of the original) remains. If 25% remains, then 75% has disintegrated. Given T₁/₂ = 20 minutes, the time taken for 75% disintegration is 2 × T₁/₂ = 2 × 20 minutes = 40 minutes.

Question 107hard

According to Bohr's model, the radius of the electron's orbit in the ground state of a hydrogen atom is approximately:

  1. 0.529 Å
  2. 1.058 Å
  3. 0.264 Å
  4. 2.116 Å
Show answer

Answer: 0.529 Å

The radius of the nth orbit in Bohr's model for a hydrogen-like atom is given by r_n = (n²h²ε₀) / (πme²Z). For the ground state of a hydrogen atom, n=1 and Z=1. Substituting the values of h, ε₀, π, m, and e, the calculated value for the first Bohr orbit (Bohr radius, a₀) is approximately 0.529 × 10⁻¹⁰ m, which is 0.529 Å.

Question 108hard

A current of 1 A flows through a conductor for 1 second. The number of electrons flowing through the conductor is approximately:

  1. 6.25 x 10^18
  2. 1.6 x 10^-19
  3. 1
  4. 6.022 x 10^23
Show answer

Answer: 6.25 x 10^18

The charge (Q) flowing through a conductor is given by Q = It, where I is the current and t is the time. Here, I = 1 A and t = 1 s, so Q = 1 C. The charge of a single electron (e) is approximately 1.6 x 10^-19 C. The number of electrons (n) is given by n = Q/e = 1 C / (1.6 x 10^-19 C/electron) ≈ 6.25 x 10^18 electrons.

Question 109hard

Which of the following is NOT a property of electromagnetic waves?

  1. They are transverse in nature.
  2. They can travel through a vacuum.
  3. They require a material medium for propagation.
  4. They travel with the speed of light in vacuum.
Show answer

Answer: They require a material medium for propagation.

Electromagnetic waves are unique in that they do not require a material medium for their propagation. They can travel through a vacuum, unlike sound waves or water waves. They are transverse, meaning the electric and magnetic field oscillations are perpendicular to the direction of propagation, and they travel at the speed of light in a vacuum.

Question 110hard

  1. Reflection
  2. Refraction
  3. Dispersion
  4. Diffraction
Show answer

Answer: Dispersion

Dispersion is the phenomenon where white light, which is a combination of different colours, splits into its constituent colours (VIBGYOR) when it passes through a prism. Question 111hard

In a Young's Double Slit Experiment (YDSE), the intensity of light at a point on the screen where the path difference is λ/4 (λ is the wavelength of light) is I. If I₀ is the maximum intensity, then I is equal to:

  1. I₀
  2. I₀/2
  3. I₀/√2
  4. 3I₀/4
Show answer

Answer: I₀/2

The intensity at a point in YDSE is given by I = I₀ cos²(φ/2), where φ is the phase difference. The phase difference φ is related to the path difference Δx by φ = (2π/λ)Δx. Given Δx = λ/4, then φ = (2π/λ)(λ/4) = π/2. So, I = I₀ cos²( (π/2)/2 ) = I₀ cos²(π/4) = I₀ (1/√2)² = I₀/2.

Question 112hard

The energy of a photon of wavelength 400 nm is approximately:

  1. 3.1 eV
  2. 1.55 eV
  3. 6.2 eV
  4. 0.77 eV
Show answer

Answer: 3.1 eV

The energy of a photon is given by E = hc/λ. We can use the approximation E (in eV) = 1240 / λ (in nm). Given λ = 400 nm, E = 1240 / 400 = 12.4 / 4 = 3.1 eV.

Question 113hard

An electric dipole is placed in a uniform electric field. The net force on the dipole is:

  1. Always zero
  2. Always non-zero
  3. Zero only if the dipole moment is parallel to the electric field
  4. Zero only if the dipole moment is perpendicular to the electric field
Show answer

Answer: Always zero

In a uniform electric field, the force on the positive charge (+q) is F = qE in the direction of the field, and the force on the negative charge (-q) is F = -qE in the opposite direction. Since the field is uniform, these two forces are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction, so the net force on the dipole is always zero. However, a torque may act on the dipole, tending to align it with the field.

Question 114hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced completely filling the space between the plates, the capacitance becomes C'. What is the ratio C'/C?

  1. K
  2. 1/K
  3. K^2
  4. 1/K^2
Show answer

Answer: K

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor with air as dielectric is given by C = ε₀A/d, where A is the area of the plates and d is the distance between them. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced completely filling the space, the new capacitance C' becomes C' = Kε₀A/d. Therefore, the ratio C'/C = (Kε₀A/d) / (ε₀A/d) = K.

Question 115hard

A current of 2 A flows through a conductor for 10 seconds. How much charge passes through any cross-section of the conductor during this time?

  1. 0.2 C
  2. 5 C
  3. 20 C
  4. 12 C
Show answer

Answer: 20 C

The relationship between current (I), charge (Q), and time (t) is given by I = Q/t. Therefore, Q = I × t. Given I = 2 A and t = 10 s, Q = 2 A × 10 s = 20 C.

Question 116hard

A proton enters a uniform magnetic field perpendicularly. Which of the following quantities of the proton will change?

  1. Speed
  2. Kinetic energy
  3. Momentum
  4. Mass
Show answer

Answer: Momentum

When a charged particle enters a uniform magnetic field perpendicularly, the magnetic force acts perpendicular to both the velocity of the particle and the magnetic field. This force causes the particle to move in a circular path. While the speed of the particle remains constant (as the force is perpendicular to velocity, no work is done), its direction of motion continuously changes. Since momentum is a vector quantity (mass × velocity), and the direction of velocity changes, the momentum of the proton will change. Kinetic energy (1/2 mv²) depends only on speed and mass, both of which remain constant. Mass is an intrinsic property and does not change.

Question 117hard

In an AC circuit, the instantaneous voltage is given by V = V₀ sin(ωt) and the instantaneous current is given by I = I₀ sin(ωt + π/2). The circuit element is a:

  1. Resistor
  2. Inductor
  3. Capacitor
  4. Combination of resistor and inductor
Show answer

Answer: Capacitor

In the given equations, the current I leads the voltage V by a phase angle of π/2 (or 90 degrees). This phase relationship (current leading voltage by 90 degrees) is characteristic of a purely capacitive circuit. For a resistor, voltage and current are in phase. For an inductor, voltage leads current by 90 degrees. For a combination, the phase difference would be between 0 and 90 degrees.

Question 118hard

A parallel plate capacitor with air between the plates has a capacitance C. If a dielectric slab of dielectric constant K and thickness t (where t < d, d being the plate separation) is introduced between the plates, the new capacitance becomes C'. Which of the following expressions correctly relates C and C'?

  1. C' = C / (1 - (t/d)(1 - 1/K))
  2. C' = C * (1 - (t/d)(1 - 1/K))
  3. C' = C / (1 + (t/d)(1 - 1/K))
  4. C' = C * (1 + (t/d)(1 - 1/K))
Show answer

Answer: C' = C / (1 - (t/d)(1 - 1/K))

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor with air is C = ε₀A/d. When a dielectric slab of thickness t and dielectric constant K is introduced, the effective distance between the plates becomes d' = (d - t) + t/K. Therefore, the new capacitance C' = ε₀A/d'. Substituting d' and simplifying, we get C' = ε₀A / [(d - t) + t/K] = ε₀A / [d(1 - t/d) + t/K] = ε₀A / [d(1 - t/d + t/(dK))] = (ε₀A/d) / [1 - t/d + t/(dK)] = C / [1 - (t/d)(1 - 1/K)]. Thus, option A is correct.

Question 119hard

An electron is accelerated through a potential difference V. It then enters a uniform magnetic field B perpendicular to its velocity. The electron moves in a circular path of radius R. If the potential difference is doubled to 2V, what will be the new radius of the circular path?

  1. R/√2
  2. R
  3. √2R
  4. 2R
Show answer

Answer: √2R

When an electron is accelerated through a potential difference V, its kinetic energy is eV = (1/2)mv². So, the velocity v = √(2eV/m). In a uniform magnetic field, the magnetic force provides the centripetal force: evB = mv²/R. From this, the radius R = mv/(eB). Substituting the expression for v, we get R = (m/eB) * √(2eV/m) = (1/B) * √(2meV/e²). This simplifies to R = (1/B) * √(2mV/e). Thus, R is proportional to √V. If the potential difference is doubled to 2V, the new radius R' will be proportional to √(2V). Therefore, R' = R * √(2V/V) = R√2. So, the new radius will be √2R.

Question 120hard

A parallel plate capacitor has capacitance C. If the distance between the plates is halved and a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced filling the space between the plates, what will be the new capacitance?

  1. C/2K
  2. 2KC
  3. KC/2
  4. 2C/K
Show answer

Answer: 2KC

The capacitance of a parallel plate capacitor is given by C = ε₀A/d, where ε₀ is the permittivity of free space, A is the area of the plates, and d is the distance between the plates. Initially, C = ε₀A/d. When the distance between the plates is halved, the new distance d' = d/2. When a dielectric medium of dielectric constant K is introduced, the new permittivity becomes ε = Kε₀. So, the new capacitance C' will be: C' = (Kε₀)A / (d/2) C' = 2K (ε₀A/d) Since C = ε₀A/d, we can substitute C into the equation: C' = 2KC Therefore, the new capacitance will be 2KC.

Question 250easy

  1. Kinetic Energy
  2. Potential Energy
  3. Thermal Energy
  4. Electromagnetic Energy
Show answer

Answer: Kinetic Energy

Question 251easy

  1. Kinetic Energy
  2. Potential Energy
  3. Thermal Energy
  4. Electromagnetic Energy
Show answer

Answer: Potential Energy

Potential energy is the energy of position or stored energy, calculated as m * g * h, where m is mass, g is acceleration due to gravity, and h is height.

Question 341medium

A ray of light passes from a denser medium to a rarer medium. It is incident at an angle of 60 degrees. What is the angle of refraction if the refractive indices of the denser and rarer medium are 1.5 and 1.0 respectively?

  1. 30
  2. 45
  3. 60
  4. 90
Show answer

Answer: 45

Using Snell's law, n1 sin(i) = n2 sin(r), we get sin(60)/1.5 = sin(r)/1.0, which gives r = 45 degrees.

Question 342medium

The time period of a simple pendulum is given by T = 2π √(l/g). If the length of the pendulum is doubled, what will be the new time period?

  1. T
  2. T/2
  3. √2 T
  4. 2T
Show answer

Answer: 2T

Since T ∝ √l, doubling the length will increase the time period by a factor of √2, but since the relation is with the square root of length, the time period will be multiplied by √2 of √2 which is 2.

Question 347medium

  1. 100GPa
  2. 200GPa
  3. 10GPa
  4. 50GPa
Show answer

Answer: 200GPa

Young's modulus is given by Y = (F/A) / (Δl/l) = (100 / (1 * 10^-6)) / (0.01 / 1) = 200 * 10^9 Pa = 200GPa.

  3. 2100J
  4. 6300J
Show answer

Answer: 4200J

Using the formula heat = mass * specific heat capacity * temperature change, we can calculate the heat required.

  3. cannot be created or destroyed
  4. can be converted to energy
Show answer

Answer: cannot be created or destroyed

The principle of conservation of momentum states that momentum cannot be created or destroyed, only converted from one object to another.

Show answer

Answer: It is a measure of time-evolution

The wave function in quantum mechanics has a characteristic related to the time-evolution of the system, which is described by the time-dependent Schrodinger equation.

  1. 1.0
  2. 1.5
  3. 1.73
  4. 2.0
Show answer

Answer: 1.73

The refractive index is calculated using the formula sin(critical angle) = 1/n, giving n = 1.73.

Question 851medium

A wave is incident on a surface at an angle of 30 degrees from a medium with refractive index 1.2 to a medium with refractive index 1.5. What is the angle of refraction?

  1. 20 degrees
  2. 25 degrees
  3. 30 degrees
  4. 40 degrees
Show answer

Answer: 25 degrees

The angle of refraction can be calculated using Snell's law, which states that the ratio of the sines of the angles of incidence and refraction is equal to the ratio of the refractive indices of the two media.

Show answer

Answer: Gamma Emission

Gamma emission is the process where a nucleus gains or loses energy and emits or absorbs gamma radiation, resulting in a change in its nuclear energy level.

Question 930medium

A ray of light passes from a denser medium to a rarer medium. What happens to the speed of light as it passes from the denser medium to the rarer medium?

  1. Increases
  2. Decreases
  3. Remains same
  4. Becomes zero
Show answer

Answer: Increases

The speed of light increases as it passes from a denser medium to a rarer medium, according to Snell's law.
